     <p><i><b>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</b></i> is a 2016 American <a href="/wiki/Superhero_film" title="Superhero film">superhero film</a> featuring the <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> characters <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a>. Directed by <a href="/wiki/Zack_Snyder" title="Zack Snyder">Zack Snyder</a> and distributed by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros. Pictures</a>, the film is a follow-up to 2013's <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i> and is the second installment in the <a href="/wiki/DC_Extended_Universe" title="DC Extended Universe">DC Extended Universe</a>. Its screenplay was written by <a href="/wiki/Chris_Terrio" title="Chris Terrio">Chris Terrio</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_S._Goyer" title="David S. Goyer">David S. Goyer</a>, and the film stars <a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cavill" title="Henry Cavill">Henry Cavill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Eisenberg" title="Jesse Eisenberg">Jesse Eisenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diane_Lane" title="Diane Lane">Diane Lane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Fishburne" title="Laurence Fishburne">Laurence Fishburne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Irons" title="Jeremy Irons">Jeremy Irons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holly_Hunter" title="Holly Hunter">Holly Hunter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gal_Gadot" title="Gal Gadot">Gal Gadot</a>. <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> is the first live-action film to feature both Batman and Superman, as well as the first theatrical film to feature live-action portrayals of <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman" title="Wonder Woman">Wonder Woman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquaman" title="Aquaman">Aquaman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyborg_(comics)" title="Cyborg (comics)">Cyborg</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flash_(Barry_Allen)" title="Flash (Barry Allen)">Flash</a>. In the film, criminal mastermind <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luthor" title="Lex Luthor">Lex Luthor</a> manipulates Batman into a preemptive battle with Superman, whom Luthor is obsessed with defeating.</p> 
     <p>The film was announced at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a>, after the release of <i>Man of Steel</i>. Snyder stated that the film would take inspiration from the <i>Batman</i> comic book series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="The Dark Knight Returns">The Dark Knight Returns</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Frank_Miller_(comics)" title="Frank Miller (comics)">Frank Miller</a>, but clarified that it would follow an original premise. The incarnation of Batman in the film would also be different than the character's portrayal in the previous <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Trilogy" title="The Dark Knight Trilogy"><i>Batman</i> film trilogy</a>, serving as a cinematic <a href="/wiki/Reboot_(fiction)" title="Reboot (fiction)">reboot</a> of the character. The film also draws influence from the "<a href="/wiki/The_Death_of_Superman" title="The Death of Superman">Death of Superman</a>" story arc. Pre-production began at <a href="/wiki/East_Los_Angeles_College" title="East Los Angeles College">East Los Angeles College</a> in October 2013, with <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">principal photography</a> starting in May 2014 in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>. Additional filming also took place in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>.</p> 
     <p><i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> premiered at the <a href="/wiki/National_Auditorium" title="National Auditorium">Auditorio Nacional</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> on March 19, 2016. It was released in the United States on March 25, 2016, in 2D, <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a>, IMAX 3D, <a href="/wiki/4DX" title="4DX">4DX</a>, premium large formats and <a href="/wiki/70_mm_film" title="70 mm film">70 mm prints</a>. The film's North American and international box office openings set new records followed by a historic box office drop in its <a href="/wiki/Second_weekend_in_box_office_performance" title="Second weekend in box office performance">second weekend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pamelamcclintock_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pamelamcclintock-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alexosborn_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexosborn-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo.com_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo.com-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-slashfilm.com_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slashfilm.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The film received generally negative reviews from the consensus of critics.<sup id="cite_ref-newsweek.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsweek.com-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-12">[12]</a></sup></p> 
     <p></p>

     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span></h2> 
     <p>Eighteen months after the destructive attack by <a href="/wiki/General_Zod" title="General Zod">General Zod</a> in <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_(comics)" title="Metropolis (comics)">Metropolis</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a> has become a controversial figure. <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Planet" title="Daily Planet">Daily Planet</a></i> journalist <a href="/wiki/Clark_Kent" title="Clark Kent">Clark Kent</a>, Superman's alter ego, has moved in with <a href="/wiki/Lois_Lane" title="Lois Lane">Lois Lane</a>. Billionaire Bruce Wayne, who has operated in <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> as <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a> for nearly two decades, sees Superman as a potential threat to humanity. After learning of Batman's activities, Superman also views him as a threat, and seeks to stop him via the <i>Daily Planet</i> articles under his disguise.</p> 
     <p>Wayne learns that Russian weapon-trafficker <a href="/wiki/KGBeast" title="KGBeast">Anatoli Knyazev</a> has been contacting <a href="/wiki/LexCorp" title="LexCorp">LexCorp</a>'s mogul <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luthor" title="Lex Luthor">Lex Luthor</a>. Meanwhile, Luthor tries to convince Senator June Finch to allow him to import <a href="/wiki/Kryptonite" title="Kryptonite">Kryptonite</a> retrieved from the Indian Ocean following the results of Zod's <a href="/wiki/Terraform" title="Terraform" class="mw-redirect">terraforming</a> attempt, claiming to use it as a "deterrent" against Kryptonians. He also makes side dealings with Finch's subordinate and demands access to Zod's body and the Kryptonian scout ship. In the next meeting with Luthor, Finch denies his import request.</p> 
     <p>Wayne attends Luthor's party at LexCorp, where he meets mysterious antiques dealer <a href="/wiki/Diana_Prince" title="Diana Prince">Diana Prince</a>, and retrieves data from the company's mainframe. The data drive, however, is stolen by Prince, who later returns it to Wayne after she is unable to decrypt the data. While decrypting the drive at the Batcave, Wayne has a dream of a post-apocalyptic world, where he leads a group of rebels against Superman. He is snapped out of the dream by a mysterious time traveler, who warns him of Lane's crucial role in the distant future, and urges him to find "the others". Wayne later realizes that Luthor is not only experimenting with Kryptonite, but also investigating <a href="/wiki/Metahuman" title="Metahuman">metahumans</a>. One of them is Prince herself, who is an immortal warrior. Wayne admits to <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a> that he plans to steal the Kryptonite to weaponize it, should it become necessary to fight Superman. Batman pursues the convoy carrying the Kryptonite from the <i>White Portuguese</i> ship to LexCorp, but Superman interferes and orders him to cease his activities.</p> 
     <p>Luthor orchestrates a bombing at a congressional hearing where Finch is questioning Superman on the validity of his actions, including a rescue of Lane in Africa where people were killed. The bomb kills dozens of people, including Finch. Frustrated with failing to save people, Superman goes into self-imposed exile. Batman breaks into LexCorp and steals the Kryptonite, planning to use it to battle Superman by building a powerful <a href="/wiki/Powered_exoskeleton" title="Powered exoskeleton">exoskeleton</a> and creating a <a href="/wiki/Grenade_launcher" title="Grenade launcher">Kryptonite grenade launcher</a> and a Kryptonite-tipped <a href="/wiki/Spear" title="Spear">spear</a>. Meanwhile, Luthor enters the Kryptonian ship and learns of its functions, as well as recorded alien worlds.</p> 
     <p>Luthor kidnaps <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_and_Martha_Kent" title="Jonathan and Martha Kent">Martha Kent</a>, Clark's adoptive mother. He reveals that he has been manipulating Batman and Superman to heighten their animosity toward each other. Luthor forces Superman to fight and kill Batman in exchange for Martha's life. Superman tries to reason with Batman, but Batman instigates a fight and ultimately gains the upper hand. Before Batman can kill Superman with the spear, Superman urges Batman to "save Martha", whose name is also shared with Wayne's <a href="/wiki/Martha_Wayne" title="Martha Wayne">late mother</a>. Lane arrives and explains the situation, making Batman realize that he and Superman are on the same side. Upon learning of Luthor's plan, Batman leaves to rescue Martha, while Superman confronts Luthor on the scout ship. Luthor unleashes a monstrous creature created from Zod's body spliced with Luthor's <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a>. Superman, Batman and Prince join forces to fight the creature, but are outmatched by its ability to absorb energy. Realizing that it is vulnerable to Kryptonite, Superman retrieves the Kryptonite spear and impales the creature. As it dies, the creature stabs and kills Superman with its bone protrusions.</p> 
     <p>Luthor is arrested and imprisoned. Speaking to Batman, he gloats that Superman's death has made the world vulnerable to powerful alien threats. A memorial is held for Superman in Metropolis. Kent is also declared dead and Wayne, Lane, Martha Kent, and Prince attend a private funeral for him in <a href="/wiki/Smallville_(comics)" title="Smallville (comics)">Smallville</a>. Martha gives an envelope to Lane which contains an engagement ring from Clark. After the funeral, Wayne reveals to Prince that he plans to form a team of metahumans, starting with the ones from Luthor's files, to help protect the world in Superman's absence. After they leave, a faint heartbeat echoes from Clark's coffin and the dirt around it begins to levitate.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span></h2> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a> as <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Bruce Wayne / Batman</a>: A billionaire socialite and owner of <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Enterprises" title="Wayne Enterprises">Wayne Enterprises</a> who dedicates himself to protect <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> from its criminal underworld as a highly trained, masked vigilante.<sup id="cite_ref-Affleck_is_Batman_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Affleck_is_Batman-13">[13]</a></sup> Brandon Spink portrays a young Bruce Wayne<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Cavill" title="Henry Cavill">Henry Cavill</a> as <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Kal-El / Clark Kent / Superman</a>: A <a href="/wiki/Kryptonian" title="Kryptonian">Kryptonian</a> survivor and a journalist for the <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Planet" title="Daily Planet">Daily Planet</a></i> who uses his superhuman abilities to protect the Earth.</li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lois_Lane" title="Lois Lane">Lois Lane</a>: A reporter for the <i>Daily Planet</i> and love interest of Clark Kent.<sup id="cite_ref-hrsupbat_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrsupbat-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jesse_Eisenberg" title="Jesse Eisenberg">Jesse Eisenberg</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luthor" title="Lex Luthor">Lex Luthor</a>: A sophisticated young businessman and hereditary CEO of <a href="/wiki/LexCorp" title="LexCorp">LexCorp</a> who is fixated on defeating who he considers as his <a href="/wiki/Archenemy" title="Archenemy">archenemy</a>, Superman.<sup id="cite_ref-Jesse_and_Jeremy_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jesse_and_Jeremy-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Diane_Lane" title="Diane Lane">Diane Lane</a> as <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_and_Martha_Kent" title="Jonathan and Martha Kent">Martha Kent</a>: Clark's adoptive mother.<sup id="cite_ref-hrsupbat_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrsupbat-15">[15]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Laurence_Fishburne" title="Laurence Fishburne">Laurence Fishburne</a> as <a href="/wiki/Perry_White" title="Perry White">Perry White</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Editor-in-chief" title="Editor-in-chief">editor-in-chief</a> of the <i>Daily Planet</i> and Clark and Lois' boss.<sup id="cite_ref-hrsupbat_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrsupbat-15">[15]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Irons" title="Jeremy Irons">Jeremy Irons</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a>: Bruce Wayne's butler, chief of security and trusted confidant.<sup id="cite_ref-Jesse_and_Jeremy_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jesse_and_Jeremy-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IronsRole_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IronsRole-19">[19]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Holly_Hunter" title="Holly Hunter">Holly Hunter</a> as June Finch: The <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Senators_from_Kentucky" title="List of United States Senators from Kentucky">United States Junior Senator from Kentucky</a> who heads the political arugment on Superman and his actions, and aids Luthor.<sup id="cite_ref-HunterMulveyOkamoto_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HunterMulveyOkamoto-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HunterRole_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HunterRole-21">[21]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Gal_Gadot" title="Gal Gadot">Gal Gadot</a> as <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman" title="Wonder Woman">Diana Prince / Wonder Woman</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-Gadot_is_WW_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gadot_is_WW-22">[22]</a></sup> A 5,000-year-old <a href="/wiki/Amazons_(DC_Comics)" title="Amazons (DC Comics)">Amazonian</a> princess,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and daughter of <a href="/wiki/Zeus_(DC_Comics)" title="Zeus (DC Comics)">Zeus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WW_demigod_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WW_demigod-24">[24]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Scoot_McNairy" title="Scoot McNairy">Scoot McNairy</a> as Wallace Keefe: An employee of Wayne Enterprises who is injured in the legs during the destruction of Metropolis and becomes a pawn in Lex's plan.<sup id="cite_ref-McNairyCast_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNairyCast-25">[25]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Callan_Mulvey" title="Callan Mulvey">Callan Mulvey</a> as <a href="/wiki/KGBeast" title="KGBeast">Anatoli Knyazev</a>: A Russian terrorist who works for Luthor.<sup id="cite_ref-HunterMulveyOkamoto_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HunterMulveyOkamoto-20">[20]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Tao_Okamoto" title="Tao Okamoto">Tao Okamoto</a> as <a href="/wiki/Mercy_Graves" title="Mercy Graves">Mercy Graves</a>: Luthor's assistant.<sup id="cite_ref-OkamotoCharacter_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OkamotoCharacter-26">[26]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Dean_Morgan" title="Jeffrey Dean Morgan">Jeffrey Dean Morgan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Cohan" title="Lauren Cohan">Lauren Cohan</a> portray <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Wayne" title="Thomas Wayne">Thomas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martha_Wayne" title="Martha Wayne">Martha Wayne</a>, Bruce Wayne's deceased parents,<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Wilson_(American_actor)" title="Patrick Wilson (American actor)">Patrick Wilson</a> portrays the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> in a voice role, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cassidy_(actor)" title="Michael Cassidy (actor)">Michael Cassidy</a> portrays <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Olsen" title="Jimmy Olsen">Jimmy Olsen</a>, a CIA agent,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robin_Atkin_Downes" title="Robin Atkin Downes">Robin Atkin Downes</a> portrays <a href="/wiki/Doomsday_(comics)" title="Doomsday (comics)">Doomsday</a> through motion-capture and voice-over work.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Reprising their roles from <i>Man of Steel</i> are <a href="/wiki/Harry_Lennix" title="Harry Lennix">Harry Lennix</a> as Secretary Calvin Swanwick,<sup id="cite_ref-LennixConfirmed_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LennixConfirmed-31">[31]</a></sup> Christina Wren as Major Carrie Farris,<sup id="cite_ref-Farris_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farris-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Costner" title="Kevin Costner">Kevin Costner</a> as the now-deceased <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_and_Martha_Kent" title="Jonathan and Martha Kent">Jonathan Kent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Carla_Gugino" title="Carla Gugino">Carla Gugino</a> as the Kryptonian A.I. <a href="/wiki/Kelex#Film" title="Kelex">Kelor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> The corpse of the now-deceased <a href="/wiki/General_Zod" title="General Zod">General Zod</a> also appears in the film in a crucial role, however, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shannon" title="Michael Shannon">Michael Shannon</a> did not film any scenes for the film and his corpse was created using the physique of fitness model <a href="/wiki/Greg_Plitt" title="Greg Plitt">Greg Plitt</a> and a head-shot of Shannon.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Ray_Fisher_(actor)" title="Ray Fisher (actor)">Ray Fisher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Momoa" title="Jason Momoa">Jason Momoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ezra_Miller" title="Ezra Miller">Ezra Miller</a> appear as <a href="/wiki/Cyborg_(comics)" title="Cyborg (comics)">Victor Stone / Cyborg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aquaman" title="Aquaman">Arthur Curry / Aquaman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flash_(Barry_Allen)" title="Flash (Barry Allen)">Barry Allen / The Flash</a> respectively in brief appearances, which will lead to their inclusion in the <i>Justice League</i> film.<sup id="cite_ref-FlashCast_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FlashCast-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FisherCast_37-0" class="reference"><a class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press_release-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Justice-league-members-confirmed_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Justice-league-members-confirmed-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Morton" title="Joe Morton">Joe Morton</a> has a cameo role as Silas Stone, Cyborg's father.<sup id="cite_ref-JoeMortonCast_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JoeMortonCast-44">[44]</a></sup> U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Leahy" title="Patrick Leahy">Patrick Leahy</a> makes a cameo appearance as Senator Purrington, whilst U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Stabenow" title="Debbie Stabenow">Debbie Stabenow</a> also makes a cameo.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LeahyCameo_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeahyCameo-46">[46]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_deGrasse_Tyson" title="Neil deGrasse Tyson">Neil deGrasse Tyson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soledad_O%27Brien" title="Soledad O'Brien">Soledad O'Brien</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anderson_Cooper" title="Anderson Cooper">Anderson Cooper</a>, <a Edition" home media release.<sup id="cite_ref-MaloneCast_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MaloneCast-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Entertainment-Weekly-1_48-0" class="reference"><a      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Further information: 
      <a href="/wiki/Batman_in_film#Batman_vs._Superman" title="Batman in film">Batman in film § Batman vs. Superman</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Superman_in_film#Batman_vs._Superman_.282001.E2.80.932002.29" title="Superman in film">Superman in film § Batman vs. Superman (2001–2002)</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3> 
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:25%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;"> 
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;"> 
       <div> 
        <p>"... after <i>Man of Steel</i> finished and we started talking about what would be in the next movie, I started subtly mentioning that it would be cool if he faced Batman... You're in a story meeting talking about, like, who should [Superman] fight if he fought this giant alien threat <a href="/wiki/General_Zod" title="General Zod">Zod</a> who was basically his equal physically, from his planet, fighting on our turf... You know, who to fight next?... But I'm not gonna say at all that when I took the job to do <i>Man of Steel</i> that I did it in a subversive way to get to Batman. I really believe that only after contemplating who could face [Superman] did Batman come into the picture."</p> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">— Snyder, on how Batman came into the film<sup id="cite_ref-Snyder_on_Batman_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Snyder_on_Batman-50">[50]</a></sup></cite>
     </div> 
     <p>In June 2013, Warner Bros. announced that director Zack Snyder and screenwriter David S. Goyer would return for a <i>Man of Steel</i> sequel,<sup id="cite_ref-BeallReplaced_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeallReplaced-51">[51]</a></sup> with the studio considering a 2015 release for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-2014Release_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014Release-52">[52]</a></sup> The following month, Snyder confirmed at <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a> that the sequel to <i>Man of Steel</i> would feature <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a> meeting for the first time in a cinematic format. Goyer and Snyder would co-write the story, with Goyer authoring the script,<sup id="cite_ref-hrsupbat_15-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hrsupbat-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sperling1_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sperling1-53">[53]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a> involved in an advisory role as executive producer.<sup id="cite_ref-Abid_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abid-54">[54]</a></sup> According to Snyder, the film would take inspiration from the comic <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Returns" title="The Dark Knight Returns">The Dark Knight Returns</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-TDKR_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TDKR-55">[55]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In November 2013, Snyder clarified that the film would not be based on the graphic novel. "If you were going to do that, you would need a different Superman. We’re bringing Batman into the universe that now this Superman lives in."<sup id="cite_ref-NotAnAdaptation_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NotAnAdaptation-56">[56]</a></sup> <i>Batman v Superman</i> marks the first appearance of <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman" title="Wonder Woman">Wonder Woman</a> in a live-action, theatrical film,<sup id="cite_ref-Gadot_is_WW_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gadot_is_WW-22">[22]</a></sup> which Warner Bros. had been developing as far back as 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-WW1996_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WW1996-57">[57]</a></sup> In December 2013, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Terrio" title="Chris Terrio">Chris Terrio</a> was hired to rewrite the script, due to Goyer's commitments to other projects. Terrio had previously collaborated with Affleck on <i><a href="/wiki/Argo_(2012_film)" title="Argo (2012 film)">Argo</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-TerrioIn_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TerrioIn-58">[58]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The film's official title, <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i>, was revealed in May 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficialTitle_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficialTitle-59">[59]</a></sup> Snyder stated that having the "v" in the title instead of "vs." was a way "to keep it from being a straight 'versus' movie, even in the most subtle way".<sup id="cite_ref-VNotVersus_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VNotVersus-60">[60]</a></sup> Henry Cavill later stated, "I wouldn't call this a Superman sequel [...] This is Batman versus Superman. It's a separate entity altogether. It's introducing the Batman character and expanding upon the universe, which was kicked off by <i>Man of Steel</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-CavillNotSupermanSequel_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CavillNotSupermanSequel-61">[61]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> noted that although the film originated as a sequel to <i>Man of Steel</i>, it was "revamped into a backdoor pilot for Justice League and/or an eventual stand-alone Batman movie."<sup id="cite_ref-ForbesJL_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ForbesJL-62">[62]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casting">Casting</span></h3>

        <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Henry_Cavill" title="Henry Cavill">Henry Cavill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Costner" title="Kevin Costner">Kevin Costner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diane_Lane" title="Diane Lane">Diane Lane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Fishburne" title="Laurence Fishburne">Laurence Fishburne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Lennix" title="Harry Lennix">Harry Lennix</a> and Christina Wren reprise their roles from <i>Man of Steel</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-LennixConfirmed_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LennixConfirmed-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Farris_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farris-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WB_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB-63">[63]</a></sup> Joining the cast are <a href="/wiki/Ben_Affleck" title="Ben Affleck">Ben Affleck</a> as <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gal_Gadot" title="Gal Gadot">Gal Gadot</a> as <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman" title="Wonder Woman">Wonder Woman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Eisenberg" title="Jesse Eisenberg">Jesse Eisenberg</a> as <a href="/wiki/Lex_Luthor" title="Lex Luthor">Lex Luthor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Irons" title="Jeremy Irons">Jeremy Irons</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Pennyworth" title="Alfred Pennyworth">Alfred Pennyworth</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-WB_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WB-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ray_Fisher_(actor)" title="Ray Fisher (actor)">Ray Fisher</a> as <a href="/wiki/Cyborg_(comics)" title="Cyborg (comics)">Cyborg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FisherCast_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FisherCast-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jason_Momoa" title="Jason Momoa">Jason Momoa</a> as <a href="/wiki/Aquaman" title="Aquaman">Aquaman</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MomoaCast_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MomoaCast-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-press_release_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-press_release-39">[39]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tao_Okamoto" title="Tao Okamoto">Tao Okamoto</a> as Luthor's assistant <a href="/wiki/Mercy_Graves" title="Mercy Graves">Mercy Graves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OkamotoCharacter_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OkamotoCharacter-26">[26]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Scoot_McNairy" title="Scoot McNairy">Scoot McNairy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Callan_Mulvey" title="Callan Mulvey">Callan Mulvey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jena_Malone" title="Jena Malone">Jena Malone</a> were cast in unspecified roles.<sup id="cite_ref-HunterMulveyOkamoto_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HunterMulveyOkamoto-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McNairyCast_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McNairyCast-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MaloneCast_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MaloneCast-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HunterCast_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HunterCast-64">[64]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>Dawn of Justice</i> is Affleck's second film as a comic book superhero; he played <a href="/wiki/Daredevil_(Marvel_Comics)" title="Daredevil (Marvel Comics)">Daredevil</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Daredevil_(film)" title="Daredevil (film)">2003 film of the same name</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-AffleckDaredevil_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AffleckDaredevil-65">[65]</a></sup> and was initially reluctant to accept playing Batman, citing that he "felt [I] didn't fit the traditional mold. But once Zack showed me the concept, and that it would be both different from the great movies that <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Chris[topher Nolan]</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christian_Bale" title="Christian Bale">Christian [Bale]</a> made, but still in keeping with tradition, I was excited."<sup id="cite_ref-AffleckReluctant_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AffleckReluctant-66">[66]</a></sup> Affleck previously stated in 2006 that <i>Daredevil</i> had "inoculated myself from ever playing another superhero".<sup id="cite_ref-AffleckNoSuperheroes_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AffleckNoSuperheroes-67">[67]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Snyder also felt that casting an older Batman would be a layered juxtaposition to a younger Superman, while "bear[ing] the scars of a seasoned crime fighter, but retain[ing] the charm that the world sees in billionaire Bruce Wayne."<sup id="cite_ref-Affleck_is_Batman_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Affleck_is_Batman-13">[13]</a></sup> Nolan was involved with the casting of Affleck and he was the first actor Snyder approached for the part.<sup id="cite_ref-Abid_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abid-54">[54]</a></sup> The director had also discussed the part with <a href="/wiki/Josh_Brolin" title="Josh Brolin">Josh Brolin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Brolin_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brolin-68">[68]</a></sup> Bale admitted he wanted to play Batman again after <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-BaleReturn_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaleReturn-69">[69]</a></sup> though he stated that his Batman does not belong in any other film and he was never approached by Warner Bros. to play the role again.<sup id="cite_ref-BaleIGN_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BaleIGN-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Snyder commented on casting Eisenberg as Luthor, "Having Jesse in the role allows us to explore that interesting dynamic, and also take the character in some new and unexpected directions".<sup id="cite_ref-Jesse_and_Jeremy_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jesse_and_Jeremy-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Olga_Kurylenko" title="Olga Kurylenko">Olga Kurylenko</a> was considered for the role of Wonder Woman before Gadot was cast.<sup id="cite_ref-KurylenkoGadot_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KurylenkoGadot-72">[72]</a></sup> Producer Charles Roven revealed that this incarnation of Wonder Woman would use the <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman#The_New_52" title="Wonder Woman">character's origins</a> in <a href="/wiki/The_New_52" title="The New 52">The New 52</a>, wherein the character would be a demigoddess, and the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Zeus_(DC_Comics)" title="Zeus (DC Comics)">Zeus</a>. This deviates from the character's original origins, where she was "a clay figure brought to life by the gods".<sup id="cite_ref-WW_demigod_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WW_demigod-24">[24]</a></sup> <i>Dawn of Justice</i> is Ray Fisher's feature film debut,<sup id="cite_ref-FisherDebut_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FisherDebut-73">[73]</a></sup> and the first live-action film to feature Cyborg,<sup id="cite_ref-CyborgDebut_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CyborgDebut-74">[74]</a></sup> whose role will become more significant in future DC Comics films.<sup id="cite_ref-CyborgSignificance_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CyborgSignificance-75">[75]</a></sup> It is also the live-action theatrical debut of Aquaman.<sup id="cite_ref-AquamanDebut_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AquamanDebut-76">[76]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The casting of Affleck, Gadot, and Eisenberg was criticized. Affleck's casting caused significant backlash from comic book fans, with multiple online petitions demanding his removal from the role; unlike previous Batman actors, he was not considered intimidating enough for the role by the protestors.<sup id="cite_ref-AffleckBacklash_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AffleckBacklash-77">[77]</a></sup> Via social media, fans criticized Gadot's small frame in contrast to Wonder Woman's warrior-like build in the comics.<sup id="cite_ref-GadotBacklash_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GadotBacklash-78">[78]</a></sup> Responding to this, Gadot stated that she had been participating in various training regimens to achieve a body that stays closer to the source material.<sup id="cite_ref-GadotResponse_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GadotResponse-79">[79]</a></sup> Fans also criticized Eisenberg's casting, feeling that the then-30-year-old was too young for the role, and not physically imposing enough.<sup id="cite_ref-EisenbergBacklash_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EisenbergBacklash-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Cranston" title="Bryan Cranston">Bryan Cranston</a> was considered for the role of Lex Luthor before Eisenberg was cast.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Design">Design</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Michael_Wilkinson_(costume_designer)" title="Michael Wilkinson (costume designer)">Michael Wilkinson</a> reprised his duties as costume designer. He updated the Superman suit from <i>Man of Steel</i> slightly so that it "feels fresh and right for this installment of Zack Snyder's comic-book universe".<sup id="cite_ref-SupermanUpdate_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SupermanUpdate-82">[82]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Batsuit" title="Batsuit">Batsuit</a> featured in the film is influenced by the one seen in <i>The Dark Knight Returns</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-BatsuitTDKR_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BatsuitTDKR-83">[83]</a></sup> unlike the suits seen in previous live-action Batman films, it is made of cloth instead of armor and is a cast of the physique of fitness model Rossano Rea.<sup id="cite_ref-BatsuitCloth_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BatsuitCloth-84">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> An image of the Wonder Woman costume was revealed at the 2014 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con</a>, in which the costume desaturates the red, blue, and gold colors that make up the costume of most versions of the character.<sup id="cite_ref-WWCostumeReveal_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WWCostumeReveal-86">[86]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A second Batsuit was also unveiled at Comic-Con, and unlike the first, it is armored.<sup id="cite_ref-BatsuitArmored_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BatsuitArmored-87">[87]</a></sup> Aquaman's look in this film, unlike most versions of the character which show him in a bright orange and green wetsuit, shows him "tattooed in <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_people" title="M?ori people">Maori</a>-like patterns", and wearing a suit "decked out in shades of gold, black and silver armor".<sup id="cite_ref-AquamanLook_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AquamanLook-88">[88]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> Studios lot, the next generation <a href="/wiki/Batmobile" title="Batmobile">Batmobile</a> combined inspiration from both the sleek, streamlined design of classic Batmobiles and the high-suspension, military build from the more recent Tumbler from the <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Trilogy" title="The Dark Knight Trilogy"><i>Dark Knight</i> Trilogy</a>. Designed by production designer <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Tatopoulos" title="Patrick Tatopoulos">Patrick Tatopoulos</a>, the Batmobile is about 20 feet long and 12 feet wide.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span></h3> 
     <p>In September 2013, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Fong" title="Larry Fong">Larry Fong</a> joined the crew as <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">cinematographer</a>, having previously worked with Zack Snyder on <i><a href="/wiki/300_(film)" title="300 (film)">300</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Watchmen_(film)" title="Watchmen (film)">Watchmen</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Sucker_Punch_(2011_film)" title="Sucker Punch (2011 film)">Sucker Punch</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-LarryFong_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LarryFong-90">[90]</a></sup> Initial filming commenced on October 19, 2013, at <a href="/wiki/East_Los_Angeles_College" title="East Los Angeles College">East Los Angeles College</a>, to shoot an American football game between <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> University and rival <a href="/wiki/Metropolis_(comics)" title="Metropolis (comics)">Metropolis</a> State University.<sup id="cite_ref-vasquez1_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vasquez1-91">[91]</a></sup> At the end of the month, construction began on the Kent farm seen in <i>Man of Steel</i> for the film.<sup id="cite_ref-KentFarm_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KentFarm-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> involving the main cast of the film began on May 19, 2014, in <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">Detroit, Michigan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FilmingBegins_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmingBegins-93">[93]</a></sup> with scenes featuring Gal Gadot as Diana Prince being filmed early on May 16.<sup id="cite_ref-GadotEarly_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GadotEarly-94">[94]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Additional filming began in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago, Illinois</a> in November 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Chicago_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chicago-95">[95]</a></sup> Other locations included the Michigan Motion Picture Studios, the <a href="/wiki/Eli_and_Edythe_Broad_Art_Museum" title="Eli and Edythe Broad Art Museum">Eli and Edythe Broad Art Museum</a> at <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">Michigan State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorkville,_Illinois" title="Yorkville, Illinois">Yorkville, Illinois</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FilmingLocations_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FilmingLocations-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worldwide_release_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldwide_release-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CanadaFilming_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CanadaFilming-98">[98]</a></sup> Sequences of the film, including a scene depicting the murder of Bruce Wayne's parents, were filmed using <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> cameras.<sup id="cite_ref-IMAXCams_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXCams-99">[99]</a></sup> The planned shoot in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> was shifted to New Mexico due to incidents related to the <a href="/wiki/2014_Ebola_outbreak" title="2014 Ebola outbreak" class="mw-redirect">2014 Ebola outbreak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MoroccoToNM_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoroccoToNM-100">[100]</a></sup> Principal photography <a href="/wiki/Wrap_(filmmaking)" title="Wrap (filmmaking)">wrapped</a> on December 5, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-ProductionEnds_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionEnds-101">[101]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Batman_v_Superman:_Dawn_of_Justice_(soundtrack)" title="Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice (soundtrack)">Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice (soundtrack)</a>
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a> returned from <i>Man of Steel</i> to compose the film score,<sup id="cite_ref-Hans_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hans-102">[102]</a></sup> emphasizing a challenge to not reuse the themes he established with the Batman character from <a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Trilogy" title="The Dark Knight Trilogy">Christopher Nolan's trilogy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HansReuse_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HansReuse-103">[103]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Junkie_XL" title="Junkie XL">Junkie XL</a>, who provided additional music in <i>Man of Steel,</i> also returned for this film, helping to compose the theme for Batman.<sup id="cite_ref-JunkieXL_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JunkieXL-104">[104]</a></sup> Originally, Zimmer enlisted Junkie XL to compose the Batman material, with Zimmer planning to focus solely on the Superman side of the score, but the final Batman theme was written by both composers as a collaboration.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Zimmer noted that he had significant trouble in finding a new angle from which to tell the story, and after the movie's release announced that he was "retiring" from superhero movies.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The soundtrack album for the score was released on March 18, 2016, via the Water Tower Music label.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span></h2> 
     <p>In January 2014, Warner Bros. announced that <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> was delayed from its original release date of July 17, 2015, and moved to May 6, 2016, in order to give the filmmakers "time to realize fully their vision, given the complex visual nature of the story."<sup id="cite_ref-YearDelay_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YearDelay-108">[108]</a></sup> The release date was moved once again in August 2014 from May 6, 2016, to March 25, 2016, with a Warner Bros. insider saying the studio was "not flinching" in regards to the previous opening date being on the same day as <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Studios" title="Marvel Studios">Marvel Studios</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America:_Civil_War" title="Captain America: Civil War">Captain America: Civil War</a></i>, but instead stating that March 2016 was a "fantastic corridor" for them.<sup id="cite_ref-NewUSRelease_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewUSRelease-109">[109]</a></sup> According to sources obtained by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i>, Warner Bros. considered the possibility of having a <a href="/wiki/70_mm_film" title="70 mm film">70mm</a> release for the film, which was partially shot in the <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">65mm IMAX</a> format.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> premiered at <a href="/wiki/National_Auditorium" title="National Auditorium">Auditorio Nacional</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> on March 19, 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> followed by a New York City premiere on March 20 at <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/2016_Brussels_bombings" title="2016 Brussels bombings">Brussels attacks</a>, Warner Bros. originally cancelled the red carpet of the London premiere, but decided to carry on with the premiere for the fans.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The film was released in the United States and the United Kingdom on March 25 in <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewUSRelease_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewUSRelease-109">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UKRelease_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKRelease-114">[114]</a></sup> It opened simultaneously in North America, China and Japan, the world's three largest film markets, as well as additional international territories,<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> with the exception of Poland, where theaters do not open on <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HigherBudget_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HigherBudget-2">[2]</a></sup> The film debuted simultaneously across 30,000 screens in nearly every major foreign territory across 61 markets, including China, with domestic open across roughly 4,242 locations of which 3,500 theaters (85%) were in 3D, 390 IMAX screens, 470 PLF locations, 150 <a href="/wiki/D-Box_Technologies" title="D-Box Technologies">D-Box</a> theaters and ten 70&nbsp;mm prints.<sup id="cite_ref-VVV_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VVV-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proj_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proj-118">[118]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>An estimated $165 million marketing effort helped promote <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-TRT_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TRT-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> At the 2014 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a>, Snyder introduced the film's first footage intended to be exclusive to the event.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> A teaser trailer was scheduled to be screened in selected cinemas on April 20, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> However, on April 16, the trailer leaked online,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> and within a few hours Snyder officially released the trailer to <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> At the 2015 San Diego Comic-Con International, Snyder and the cast attended to present an initial trailer of the film. The trailer was, unlike the teaser, which received mixed response, positively received by attendees, who gave the trailer a <a href="/wiki/Standing_ovation" title="Standing ovation">standing ovation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Mark Hughes of <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> said the trailers "both set the stage for a story about the world’s distrust and fear of Superman, Batman’s rage at Superman and intention to duke it out with the Man of Steel, and Wonder Woman’s participation in a big fight featuring the 'Trinity.'"<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Warner Bros. Consumer Products partnered-up with "a powerhouse slate of global licensees for a broad, multi-category licensing and merchandising program", including <a href="/wiki/Mattel" title="Mattel">Mattel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a>, Rubies, <a href="/wiki/Funko" title="Funko">Funko</a>, Thinkway Toys, <a href="/wiki/Hot_Toys" title="Hot Toys">Hot Toys</a>, Junkfood, Bioworld, <a href="/wiki/Pez" title="Pez">Pez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seiko" title="Seiko">Seiko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a> and among many other licensees to sell merchandise related to the film.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fiat_Chrysler_Automobiles" title="Fiat Chrysler Automobiles">Fiat Chrysler Automobiles</a> was also a licensee for the film, offering a special edition <a href="/wiki/Jeep_Renegade" title="Jeep Renegade" class="mw-disambig">Jeep Renegade</a><sup class="plainlinks noprint Inline-Template" style="vertical-align:text-top;white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://dispenser.homenet.org/~dispenser/cgi-bin/dab_solver.py?page=Batman_v_Superman:_Dawn_of_Justice&amp;editintro=Template:Disambiguation_needed/editintro&amp;client=Template:Dn"><span title="Link needs disambiguation. (March 2016)">disambiguation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in exchange for a near-exclusive <a href="/wiki/Product_placement" title="Product placement">product placement</a> deal; aside from Bruce Wayne's <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a>, all vehicles in the film were either from <a href="/wiki/Chrysler_(division)" title="Chrysler (division)">Chrysler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodge" title="Dodge">Dodge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeep" title="Jeep">Jeep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ram_Trucks" title="Ram Trucks">Ram</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Iveco" title="Iveco">Iveco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice – Cross Fire</i>, an original companion novel tied to the film, telling a tie-in story set before the events of the movie, was published by <a href="/wiki/Scholastic_Corporation" title="Scholastic Corporation">Scholastic Corporation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A five-issue comic-book prelude exploring what happened in the weeks and months leading up to the events of the film was released as a tie-in with <a href="/wiki/Dr_Pepper" title="Dr Pepper">Dr Pepper</a>'s character-branded bottles.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Also, there are a series of four <a href="/wiki/Minicomic" title="Minicomic">minicomics</a> found in <i>Batman v Superman</i>-branded <a href="/wiki/General_Mills" title="General Mills">General Mills</a> cereals. Additionally, those who purchased <i>Batman v Superman</i>-themed <a href="/wiki/Doritos" title="Doritos">Doritos</a> Family Fun Mix at <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> received the comic book prequel <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice – Upstairs/Downstairs</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rocksteady_Studios" title="Rocksteady Studios">Rocksteady Studios</a> released a <a href="/wiki/Downloadable_content" title="Downloadable content">downloadable content</a> for the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Batman:_Arkham_Knight" title="Batman: Arkham Knight">Batman: Arkham Knight</a></i> that featured the Batmobile and Batsuit from the film.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The third trailer debuted on <i><a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live!" title="Jimmy Kimmel Live!">Jimmy Kimmel Live!</a></i> on December 3, 2015. It received positive responses,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> with Scott Mendelson of <i>Forbes</i> calling the trailer a "Saturday morning cartoon nerd’s wildest dreams."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> Molly Driscoll of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">CS Monitor</a></i> stated that it looks like the film "will continue the trend of adapting comic book stories as timely tales."<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Graeme McMillan of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> noted that based on the trailer's content, the film might be the anti-<i>Civil War</i>, referring to Marvel's <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_America:_Civil_War" title="Captain America: Civil War">Captain America: Civil War</a></i> as "Superman and Batman complete the comic book trope by overcoming their differences to fight a common foe, alongside a third hero, who saves them both — that feels the most fresh, especially in light of the <i>Civil War</i> trailer. While that ended with a showdown between three heroes, this trailer moves beyond that to show three heroes standing united."<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> However, some criticised it exactly for revealing that,<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> with Rob Tornoe of <i><a href="/wiki/WHYY-FM" title="WHYY-FM">NewsWorks</a></i> pointing out that this trailer was targeting the "broadest audience" rather than just fans, as studios try to "maximize a film's opening day box office."<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg/220px-Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg/330px-Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg/440px-Atat%C3%BCrk_Havaliman%C4%B1nda_T%C3%BCrk_Hava_Yollar%C4%B1_Boeing_777_Batman_S%C3%BCpermen%27e_kar%C5%9F%C4%B1_logojet.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853"></a>
