        </div> An advertisement for the film on 
        <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>' 
        <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-300ER</a> at 
        <a href="/wiki/Istanbul_Atat%C3%BCrk_Airport" title="Istanbul Atatürk Airport">Istanbul Atatürk Airport</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Warner Bros. did not buy a <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_50" title="Super Bowl 50">Super Bowl 50</a> commercial;<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> instead, they worked with <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a> to put together a pair of <i>Batman v Superman</i>-themed airline commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-BvS-TAC_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BvS-TAC-143">[143]</a></sup> McMillan of <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> stated that the spots "inform interested parties about the culture, geography and history of Batman and Superman's individual stomping grounds, each one filled with <a href="/wiki/Easter_egg_(media)" title="Easter egg (media)">Easter eggs</a> for the comic book faithful and newcomer alike."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> Jesse Eisenberg's part as Lex Luthor in these commercials was praised, as Dirk Libbey of <i>CinemaBlend</i> noted that "he matches up well with Bruce Wayne by playing the welcoming billionaire business man. It's a far cry from the somewhat cartoonish villain we’ve seen in the clips from the film."<sup id="cite_ref-BvS-TAC_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BvS-TAC-143">[143]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The final trailer was released on February 11, 2016, which was described as "intense" by Kwame Opam of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Verge" title="The Verge">The Verge</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> Mendelson of <i>Forbes</i> felt that Warner Bros. "probably wouldn’t have even dropped this one had the prior trailer back in December been received better. So now we have this fourth and final sell, and at least they are going out on a high note."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Jonathon Dornbush of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> said that the footage "works to establish Batman as his own independent crime fighting force, while also providing a deeper look at his existential struggle against Superman."<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In February 2016, Warner Bros. and Doritos formed a partnership, creating a website offering fans the opportunity to enter codes found on Doritos purchases branded with the film's logo, and enter to win movie tickets, tech toys, and a trip the premiere in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> Warner Bros also partnered with <a href="/wiki/Omaze" title="Omaze">Omaze</a> to give fans who donated a chance to win "The Ultimate <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> Experience", while benefiting three nonprofit organizations nominated by Ben Affleck, Henry Cavill and Jesse Eisenberg. "The Ultimate <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> Experience" offered a fan and their friend the chance to win tickets to the premiere of the film, as well as fly on a helicopter with Cavill or ride in the Batmobile with Affleck.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hendrick_Motorsports" title="Hendrick Motorsports">Hendrick Motorsports</a> drivers <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Johnson" title="Jimmie Johnson">Jimmie Johnson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dale_Earnhardt,_Jr." title="Dale Earnhardt, Jr.">Dale Earnhardt, Jr</a>. drove cars based on Superman and Batman respectively, at <a href="/wiki/Auto_Club_Speedway" title="Auto Club Speedway">Auto Club Speedway</a> on March 20, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span></h3> 
     <p>An <i>Ultimate Edition</i> of the film featuring extended content will be released on home media. The version received an R-rating from the <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" title="Motion Picture Association of America">Motion Picture Association of America</a>, for more violence than the PG-13 rated theatrical cut,<sup id="cite_ref-Entertainment-Weekly-1_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Entertainment-Weekly-1-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> and will be 30 minutes longer than the theatrical version.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> It was announced that the Blu-ray will be released on July 16, 2016 with both a PG-13 and R rating versions.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span></h3> 
     <p>The film grossed $166 million in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a> in its opening weekend,<sup id="cite_ref-debut-lower_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debut-lower-155">[155]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dominates-B.O._156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dominates-B.O.-156">[156]</a></sup> the seventh biggest opening of all-time, ahead of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a>'</i> $160.9 million.<sup id="cite_ref-debut-lower_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debut-lower-155">[155]</a></sup> The film had a worldwide opening of $422.5 million, which stands as the biggest opening for a superhero film, the second biggest for Warner Bros. and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_films" title="List of highest-grossing openings for films">fourth biggest of all-time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> It became just the fourth film to have a global opening above $400 million.<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup> It also had an IMAX worldwide opening weekend total of $36 million from 945 IMAX screens, the third biggest ever, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i> ($48 million) and <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_World" title="Jurassic World">Jurassic World</a></i> ($44 million).<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup> However, both inside and outside of the United States, <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> experienced a notable poor Friday-to-Sunday hold and set a new record for the worst Friday-to-Sunday drop for a superhero movie release in modern box office history with a 58% decline, which was previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Four_(2015_film)" title="Fantastic Four (2015 film)">Fantastic Four</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Worst_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worst-159">[159]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In its <a href="/wiki/Second_weekend_in_box_office_performance" title="Second weekend in box office performance">second weekend</a>, <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> experienced a "historic" box-office drop,<sup id="cite_ref-pamelamcclintock_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pamelamcclintock-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alexosborn_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexosborn-6">[6]</a></sup> with a 81.2% decline on Friday that was "one of the biggest Friday-to-Friday drops any blockbuster has ever seen", and an overall "68.4%" drop for the weekend despite not "facing any big competition at the box office",<sup id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo.com1_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo.com1-160">[160]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo.com_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo.com-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-slashfilm.com_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-slashfilm.com-8">[8]</a></sup> making it the second largest decline for a marquee superhero title rivaled only by 2003's <i><a href="/wiki/Hulk_(film)" title="Hulk (film)">Hulk</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-pamelamcclintock_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pamelamcclintock-5">[5]</a></sup> Brad Brevet, writing for <a href="/wiki/Box_Office_Mojo" title="Box Office Mojo">Box Office Mojo</a>, reported, "it appeared <i>Batman v Superman</i> was looking at a drop anywhere from 58-68% and it ended up settling in on the wrong side of those expectations."<sup id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo.com1_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo.com1-160">[160]</a></sup> Scott Mendelson, writing for <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>, said of the film's box office decline, "Whether or not the movie is any good, and whether or not audiences respond to the picture, is best measured by the second and third weekends...Yes, we’re still talking about a $15.35 million second Friday and a $50m+ second weekend, but in terms of legs, this film sadly doesn’t seem to have any."<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Continuing this trend, in its third weekend the film dropped by 54.3% in which Brad Brevet, in a follow-up for <a href="/wiki/Box_Office_Mojo" title="Box Office Mojo">Box Office Mojo</a>, concluded that "the legs on this one are proving quite short."<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>With a production budget of $250 million, after rebates and tax incentives and a marketing budget of around $150–160 million,<sup id="cite_ref-TRT_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TRT-119">[119]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> estimates that the film needs to earn $800 million to recoup its investment. One media analyst, quoted by the magazine, said that given the costs and need to launch a series of future films, "anything under $1 billion in worldwide box office will be a disappointment."<sup id="cite_ref-800M_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-800M-163">[163]</a></sup> In the weeks leading up to the film's release, advance ticket sales outpaced <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Marvel%27s_The_Avengers" title="Marvel's The Avengers" class="mw-redirect">The Avengers</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Furious_7" title="Furious 7">Furious 7</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-1billion_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1billion-164">[164]</a></sup> Worldwide, it was estimated to gross between $300–340 million in over 35,000 screens in its opening weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-VVV_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VVV-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WorldwideOpening_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldwideOpening-165">[165]</a></sup> It passed the $50 million mark in IMAX ticket sales on its second weekend, grossing a total of $53.4 million from 571 IMAX screens.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas15thOpening_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas15thOpening-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BOOMBOOMBOOM_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOOMBOOMBOOM-167">[167]</a></sup> As of April 10, 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Batman_v_Superman:_Dawn_of_Justice&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> has grossed $296.6 million in North America and $487.7 million in other territories for a worldwide total of $784.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-BOM_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOM-4">[4]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span></h4> 
     <p>Following reports of pre-tickets sales in both the United States and Canada on February 29, many insiders and analysts predicted an opening weekend haul between $120–140 million for <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i>, with some projecting as high as $185 million.<sup id="cite_ref-VVV_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VVV-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proj_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proj-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WorldwideOpening_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldwideOpening-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WW_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WW-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> However, Warner Bros. insiders were more conservative in their estimates projecting in the lower range of $110 million.<sup id="cite_ref-HigherBudget_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HigherBudget-2">[2]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Deadline.com" title="Deadline.com">Deadline.com</a>, an undisclosed rival studio box office analyst indicated that if the film is truly pacing in tandem with <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, then <i>Dawn of Justice</i> could possibly be looking at a $180 million+ debut.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldwideOpening_165-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldwideOpening-165">[165]</a></sup> The film also became <a href="/wiki/Fandango_(ticket_service)" title="Fandango (ticket service)">Fandango</a>'s top pre-selling superhero film ever, beating <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Age_of_Ultron" title="Avengers: Age of Ultron">Avengers: Age of Ultron</a></i>, representing 90% of the site's weekend's ticket sales. A survey carried out showed that the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Woman" title="Wonder Woman">Wonder Woman</a> is a primary draw for moviegoers.<sup id="cite_ref-WW_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WW-169">[169]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fan_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fan-171">[171]</a></sup> It pre-sold around $20–25 million worth of advance tickets.<sup id="cite_ref-WW_169-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WW-169">[169]</a></sup> <i>Dawn of Justice</i> made $27.7 million in Thursday previews from around 3,800 theaters which is the biggest of 2016, the biggest Easter weekend preview, the second-biggest for a superhero film (behind <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>), and the seventh-biggest of all time of which $3.6 million came from IMAX showings, also a new record for Easter weekend.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Audiences polled by <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> gave the film an average grade of "B" on an A+ to F scale.<sup id="cite_ref-CinemaScore_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CinemaScore-174">[174]</a></sup> It earned "B–" from men, "B" from women, a "B from under–25 and a "B–" from those over 25.<sup id="cite_ref-SMF_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMF-175">[175]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>On its opening day, it earned $81.59 million from 4,242 theaters, including previews, marking the biggest pre-summer opening day of all time, the second-biggest superhero Friday opening and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_films#Biggest_opening_day_in_U.S._and_Canada" title="List of highest-grossing openings for films">fourth-biggest opening day and fourth-biggest single-day gross</a>, with $9 million coming from IMAX showings.<sup id="cite_ref-FFF_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFF-176">[176]</a></sup> Excluding the Thursday previews, it earned $53.89 million on Friday which is the fifth-biggest ever.<sup id="cite_ref-FFF_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFF-176">[176]</a></sup> It fell 37.8% on Saturday, which is the second worst superhero opening Friday-to-Saturday drop, only behind the 40% drop of <i>The Dark Knight Rises.</i><sup id="cite_ref-Worst_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worst-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Worst_159-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worst-159">[159]</a></sup> In total, it earned $166 million for its debut weekend, setting records for the biggest March and pre-summer opening,<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> the biggest Easter opening,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> the second biggest opening for <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> the biggest for a DC Comics property,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_openings_for_films" title="List of highest-grossing openings for films">seventh-biggest opening of all time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dominates-B.O._156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dominates-B.O.-156">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-B.O._181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-B.O.-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OP_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OP-182">[182]</a></sup> Conversely, the film holds the record for the worst superhero Friday-to-Sunday drop with a 58% decline, eclipsing the previous 48% decline record held by <i><a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Four_(2015_film)" title="Fantastic Four (2015 film)">Fantastic Four</a></i> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-Worst_159-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Worst-159">[159]</a></sup> IMAX comprised 11% or $18 million of the weekend's gross from 388 theaters which is the fifth biggest of all time (a record it shares with <i>Age of Ultron</i>) and 3D represented 40% ($68 million) of the total ticket sales.<sup id="cite_ref-SMF_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMF-175">[175]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/RealD_3D" title="RealD 3D">RealD 3D</a> comprised $47 million of the opening gross.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-B.O._181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-B.O.-181">[181]</a></sup> Premium large formats generated $17.6 million (10%), with $3.6 million of that coming from Cinemark XD auditoriums from 475 theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline-B.O._181-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-B.O.-181">[181]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Following its record breaking opening weekend, it posted the biggest March Monday with $15.05 million, a drop of 55% from its Sunday gross. This broke <i>The Hunger Games</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span> previous record of $10.8 million,<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> and also the biggest March Tuesday with $12.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-T500_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T500-185">[185]</a></sup> It made $209 million in its first week full which stands at the eleventh biggest opening week of all time<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> and surpassed the lifetime total <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Despite earning $15.35 million in its second Friday, the film dropped 81.2% and broke the record for the biggest Friday-to-Friday drop for a comic book adaptation film, not including $27.7 million worth of previews which represented an even larger decline.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> It fell precipitously by 69.1% in its <a href="/wiki/Second_weekend_in_box_office_performance" title="Second weekend in box office performance">second weekend</a>, grossing $51.3 million from 4,256 theaters (an addition of 14 cinemas) due to poor reviews and mixed <a href="/wiki/Word_of_mouth" title="Word of mouth">word of mouth</a>, establishing itself an infamous record for the seventh steepest drop for a superhero/comic book adapted film and the steepest decline since the -69% posted by <i><a href="/wiki/X-Men_Origins:_Wolverine" title="X-Men Origins: Wolverine">X-Men Origins: Wolverine</a></i> in 2009, despite facing little to no competition or new wide-releases and having the added benefit of 30% <a href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312" title="K–12">K–12</a> schools off, and 9% of colleges on break, per <a href="/wiki/ComScore" title="ComScore">ComScore</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> The steep drop also marks the fourth-biggest for a film that opened above $100 million (tied with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Twilight_Saga:_Breaking_Dawn_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="The Twilight Saga: Breaking Dawn – Part 2">The Twilight Saga: Breaking Dawn – Part 2</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-BOOMBOOMBOOM_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BOOMBOOMBOOM-167">[167]</a></sup> In its third weekend it was overtaken by the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boss_(2016_film)" title="The Boss (2016 film)">The Boss</a></i> after falling 54% with $23.3 million.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_North_America">Outside North America</span></h4> 
     <p>Internationally, it was projected to open between $180–200 million; however, Deadline.com pointed out that these figures are only early predictions that are pegged to the performance of similar films in their respective territories.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldwideOpening_165-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldwideOpening-165">[165]</a></sup> It opened Wednesday, March 23, 2016, in 10 countries, earning $7 million, where it debuted at No. 1 in all markets on roughly 5,900 screens.<sup id="cite_ref-INTopening_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INTopening-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> It opened in 38 more countries on March 24, earning $33.1 million on 19,700 screens for a two-day total of $44 million from 45 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-INTopening_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INTopening-193">[193]</a></sup> On Friday, March 25, it finally opened in its last 17 countries, where they delivered a combined total of $67.2 million, for a three-day total of $115.3 million from 62 countries on over 30,000 screens.<sup id="cite_ref-INTopening_193-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INTopening-193">[193]</a></sup> Through Sunday, March 27, it earned an opening-weekend total of $256.5 million from 66 countries on over 40,000 screens, which stands as the biggest superhero opening weekend of all time, the biggest March opening, the second biggest opening for Warner Bros. and the fifth biggest international opening ever.<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> This included the second-biggest IMAX opening record of $18 million, behind only <i><a href="/wiki/Jurassic_World" title="Jurassic World">Jurassic World</a></i> ($23.5 million).<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup> 3D accounted 59% or $149.86 million of the weekend gross led by China (98%), Germany (88%), Brazil (81%), Russia (55%), and France (51%).<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup> As with North America, the film witnessed steep decline in its second Friday internationally, falling 72% to 19.2 million from 67 countries with the biggest decline in the U.K. (77%) and China (87%),<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DLD_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DLD-197">[197]</a></sup> and fell overall 66% to $85.25 million in its second weekend from 28,000 screens in 67 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas15thOpening_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas15thOpening-166">[166]</a></sup> It topped the box office for three consecutive weekends.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas17thOpening_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas17thOpening-198">[198]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In Mexico, it had the biggest opening day for Warner Bros. and the second biggest of all time with $5.8 million, including record-breaking midnight showings.<sup id="cite_ref-INTopening_193-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INTopening-193">[193]</a></sup> It also scored the biggest opening day of all time in Brazil ($3.5 million) and the biggest opening day for a superhero film in Germany ($2.8 million).<sup id="cite_ref-Day2_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Day2-199">[199]</a></sup> Elsewhere, it opened in the United Kingdom and Ireland ($9 million), Australia ($2.5 million), India ($2.54 million), Russia ($1.9 million), South Korea ($1.7 million), Japan ($1.2 million), the United Arab Emirates and Hong Kong ($1.1 million respectively).<sup id="cite_ref-INTopening_193-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INTopening-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Day2_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Day2-199">[199]</a></sup> In China, it earned $21.22 million on its opening day, including around $1.34 million worth of previews, which is the biggest for Warner Bros. and the sixth biggest Hollywood opening day of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-INTopening_193-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-INTopening-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> However, other Chinese sources have the film open to around $20 million.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> In terms of opening weekends, the biggest openings were recorded in China ($57.2 million), the United Kingdom and Ireland ($20.7 million), Mexico ($18.2 million), Brazil ($12 million), South Korea ($10.2 million), Australia ($9.9 million), France ($8.6 million), Germany ($8.1 million), Russia ($7.7 million), India ($6.6 million), Spain ($6.1 million) and Japan ($4.5 million).<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> It broke all time opening record in Brazil and Warner Bros. opening records in Mexico, Hong Kong, India, Malaysia, Singapore, Vietnam, Argentina, Bolivia, Chile, Colombia, Peru, Puerto Rico and Venezuela.<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom and Ireland, it benefited from the long Easter weekend holiday and despite a distinctly mixed bag of reviews in the U.K. press, it posted an opening £14.62 million or $20.7 million from 612 theaters, a record for 2016 so far and for a superhero title on straight Friday to Sunday, but fell short of <i>The Avengers</i> and <i>Avengers: Age of Ultron</i>, when accounting for previews.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TG_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TG-205">[205]</a></sup> In Japan, it opened in third place, behind two local films, <i><a href="/wiki/Assassination_Classroom:_Graduation" title="Assassination Classroom: Graduation">Assassination Classroom: Graduation</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Doraemon:_Nobita_and_the_Birth_of_Japan_2016" title="Doraemon: Nobita and the Birth of Japan 2016">Doraemon: Nobita and the Birth of Japan 2016</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> In South Korea, it scored the biggest March opening after opening on a Tuesday and dominating 68.3% of the market share with $10.2 million.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> In China, after scoring the biggest Hollywood opening Friday (behind <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers:_Age_of_Extinction" title="Transformers: Age of Extinction">Transformers: Age of Extinction</a></i>),<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> it earned an estimated $57.2 million from approximately 16,000 screens in its opening weekend, besting all other DC Comics adaption film just by its weekend haul except for <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i> and gave Warner Bros. its biggest three day opening there with $7 million coming from 557 IMAX screens.<sup id="cite_ref-DeadBvS_158-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeadBvS-158">[158]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-THRChina_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-THRChina-209">[209]</a></sup> However, the opening figure fell below analysts projections of $70–80 million.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> It held the top spot for its first seven days only, after which it faced stiff competitions from local productions,<sup id="cite_ref-DLD_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DLD-197">[197]</a></sup> and fell dramatically from then onwards in accruing revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> As a result, it fell to third place in its second weekend after falling enormously by 78% to $12.7 million, a record for a superhero film. It was neck-in-neck tie with <i>Zootopia</i> for the third position.<sup id="cite_ref-Overseas15thOpening_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Overseas15thOpening-166">[166]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_response">Critical response</span></h3> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> reported that <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> received a negative reception from critics.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Review_aggregator" title="Review aggregator">Review aggregator</a> website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> reported a 28% approval rating based on 316 reviews, with an average rating of 4.9/10. The site's critical consensus reads, "<i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> smothers a potentially powerful story – and some of America's most iconic superheroes – in a grim whirlwind of effects-driven action."<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Weighted_arithmetic_mean" title="Weighted arithmetic mean">weighted average</a> to mainstream critic reviews, gave the film an average score of 44 out of 100, based on 51 critics.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> reported that, "the film had been widely praised by fans after its first screening in New York last week. But critics have not been so positive about the long-awaited movie."<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> Lindy West in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> described it as "153 minutes of a grown man whacking two dolls together", asking "(h)as the definition of 'movie' changed from 'motion picture story that a human wrote on purpose' to '700 only tangentially related 12-second grey and red vignettes'?"<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> wrote: "The point of <i>Batman v Superman</i> isn't fun, and it isn't thinking, either. It's obedience. The theology is invoked ... to buttress a spectacle of power. And in that way the film serves as a metaphor for its own aspirations. The corporations that produce movies like this one, and the ambitious hacks who sign up to make them, have no evident motive beyond their own aggrandizement."<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-219">[219]</a></sup> Writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Telegraph_(magazine)" title="The Telegraph (magazine)">The Telegraph</a></i>, Robbie Collin called the film "humorless" and "the most incoherent blockbuster in years".<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> Cynthia Fuchs of <i><a href="/wiki/PopMatters" title="PopMatters">PopMatters</a></i> said, "As you’re watching this movie, you might also contemplate your own part, in being swayed into consuming so much of what you’ve consumed before." Adding, "Wonder Woman’s remains <i>Batman v Superman</i>‘s most compelling story, precisely because it’s untold."<sup id="cite_ref-PM_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PM-221">[221]</a></sup> Matt Patches of <i><a href="/wiki/Thrillist_Media_Group" title="Thrillist Media Group">Thrillist</a></i> wrote "what <i>Batman v Superman</i> can do, it does, at the cost of coherency and thrills. The movie is bat-shit crazy. A dour, disdainful demeanor, plus a gluttony of complex plot twists, dissipates most of the contact high."<sup id="cite_ref-T_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T-222">[222]</a></sup> Michael Philips of <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> wrote, "A near-total drag, <i>Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</i> plays like a loose, unofficial quarter-billion-dollar remake of <i>The Odd Couple</i>, in which Oscar and Felix are literally trying to kill each other."<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> On his <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcast</a> <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Babble-On" title="Hollywood Babble-On">Hollywood Babble-On</a>, film director <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Smith" title="Kevin Smith">Kevin Smith</a>, a long-time friend and collaborator of Affleck, praised Affleck's performance but panned the film, commenting that it "didn’t really have a heart" and was "humorless", arguing that "there seems to be a fundamental lack of understanding of what those characters are about. It’s almost like Zack Snyder didn’t read a bunch of comics, he read one comic once, and it was <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_Knight_Returns" title="Dark Knight Returns" class="mw-redirect">Dark Knight Returns</a></i>, and his favourite part was the last part where Batman and Superman fight."<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> On a second viewing, however, Smith via his Instagram lightened his stance.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Conversely, David Betancourt of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> and Scott Mendelson of <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> praised the film's visual spectacle and the performances of Affleck, Gadot, Irons and Hunter, though Mendelson also called the film "an utter mess of thinly sketched characters, haphazard plotting, surprisingly jumbled action".<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> called the film "better than <i>Man of Steel</i> but below the high bar set by Nolan's <i>Dark Knight</i>, adding that "<i>Dawn of Justice</i> is still a colossus, the stuff that DC Comics dreams are made of for that kid in all of us who yearns to see Batman and Superman suit up and go in for the kill."<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Jake Coyle of <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> wrote, "it hurtles not with the kinetic momentum of <i>Mad Max: Fury Road</i> nor the comparatively spry skip of a Marvel movie, but with an operatic grandeur it sometimes earns and often doesn't."<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup> Mark Hughes of <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> called it "the follow-up to <i>The Dark Knight</i> that many viewers and fans wanted or hoped for", adding that it's "visually stunning, with powerful emotional storytelling and awe-inspiring action spectacle."<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> Andrew Barker of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> said "as a pure visual spectacle... <i>Batman V Superman</i> ably blows the hinges off the multiplex doors."<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> Charles Koplinski of the <i><a href="/wiki/Illinois_Times" title="Illinois Times">Illinois Times</a></i> called it "a brooding, but most importantly intelligent take on the seminal figures of our 20th century pop culture mythology, a movie that at once pays tribute to these characters' roots while offering up modern incarnations of them that ring true for our times."<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> Nicolas Barber of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> called the film "a four-star epic" praising Affleck's performance as Batman and the visual grandeur of Fong's cinematography.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> Jordan Hoffman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> praised Affleck and Gadot's performances, calling Gadot as Wonder Woman the best thing in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
